<rating>5<//rating><text>My husband and I wanted to try something new but were in the mood for garlic noodles. Found this spot on Yelp.

I got the premium bbq combo with garlic noodles and a fried egg. It came in a cute disposable bento box with pickled and steamed veggies. With a slice of pineapple delicious. Everything had great flavor and very filling.
My husband got the chili shrimp and spicy garlic noodles which were also great. We also order the super fruit organic jasmine drink and the organic mango smoothie pearl which this one reminded me of boba but with jellies instead of tapioca balls.

Overall was a great first impression and we will be coming back.<//text>< Pics>

< review>
A welcome higher end Pho restaurant in the Dublin area. Clean and modern. Upscale utensils and presentation. Good quality. The main area for improvement is in the temperature of the broth. The bowl is the same for regular or large. After mixing, the food is not warm enough, especially for the large order. Basil chicken also not hot off the fryer.<//review>

< text>
Food was great, had a ton of flavor. Portions were overly generous. I'm a big dude with a large appetite, was full halfway through my meal. Ordered vermicelli with lemon grass chicken. Came with a jalepeno chutneys, fish sauce, and a salad dressing. All house made with great flavor. The real draw though is I'm a milk tea addict. I got the Ancient Black Fresh Milk Tea. This is some of the best boba tea I've had, maybe the best. I'm not a boba person, usually omit it, just do straight tea brown sugar, or crema. Not with this tea. The boba is stupid fresh with the perfect chewiness to it.  Can't wait to try them again. And yes I would totally stop by just for tea alone. Food is just a bonus to me.</text>

< Review>
YUMMY YUM*** (low prices, homey atmosphere)

I used to live by this place, always being drawn in by the "Join the Revolution" painted on the door. It's welcoming in a nation that regularly kills its citizens with impunity, and tears families apart. To have a restaurant that overtly positions itself with a more peaceful world is something I will definitely get behind.

The regular menu is something, but to really experience this place you have to wait for their special menus. They have the most wonderful dishes that will probably only show up in LA here. I also appreciate that the prices are waaaay reasonable. I don't have to complain about how unreasonably high everything is like I do with LIT-ER-AL-LY everything else in this city.

I bring my friends here whenever they come to visit LA, it's a necessary.< /Review>

< review>
Amazing tacos. Authentic flavors. You travel the world with every bite inside a hole in the wall joint that's just well lit enough to feel romantic. The view outside is an urban appeal you will not find anywhere but LA. Portion size is perfect , sides are just right with pickled onions , radish and carrots. The spicy harissa adds the right amount of kick. The lamb and brisket were my favorite , the falafel was super tasty but needed some kind of sauce, and the duck tasted exactly like the flavors of north africa and the middle east. Loved everything about this place, except the street parking. :)<//review>

<Review>Dy-no-mite! The place is all about the food and the neighborhood. Farid hangs out on the sidewalk, smoking lamb, curing beef bacon, and roasting duck for the delicious tacos. He's always got a laugh and a hug for the customers. His partner/wife handles the operations. She makes sure everything runs smoothly and is fresh. Perfect balance.

My favorites tacos are the roasted cauliflower (don't miss it, do yourself a favor), the roast duck and potato, and the smoked lamb (what I said about the cauliflower? apply it here). When I want to eat big, I get the semolina pancakes with orange maple syrup during brunch.

All hand made condiments, drinks, and desserts. And did I mention very reasonable prices? Well, I should have. Gluten-free corn tortillas and tons of vegetarian, too.

Park on the side streets for free, in front if it's not rush hour, and enjoy yourself some North African food prepared by a French North African!< /Review><rating>5< /rating>< Pictures>

<review>Revolutionario, the birthplace of the North African Taco, is another one of my favorite Los Angeles spots. They not only have great food at reasonable prices - but they are also highly engaged with the local community (as I understand, they do work feeding the homeless). In my experience the chef and staff are friendly, engaging, and have created a space that reflects this. I've been to Revolutionario at least 5 times now, I've ordered something different each time, and the food has always been excellent and unique.

The portions look sort of small due to the way they are served but are very filling. I tend to order a "bowl" over the taco or burrito, but I wouldn't hesitate to recommend any style. Top off your dish at the sauce and toppings bar to accentuate the great medley of flavors (their harissa and yogurt sauces are fantastic). I like to pair the hot food with the sweet, fruity drinks they have available on tap.

Definitely a worthwhile local trip from anywhere in the city - or if you're visiting the USC area.< /review><username>Chad K< /username><resp>None</resp><gmapID>0x80c2c7f7c5106149:0x39f262ea2be85a5d</gmapID><userid>118340948866946722024</userid></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Revolutionario is an absolutely fantastic little gem of a local spot. When I visited I had a pleasure of meeting Chef Zadi, his staff and family and they were the most hospitable restaurant team on this earth. The vibe felt more like being at someone's backyard barbeque (albeit indoors) than a sterile & boring new restaurant.

What's fantastic are the little bites, the brics and of course, the meat and relishes. I literally sampled 7 things in one sitting without hurting my wallet and all I could do was cry in joy at the complex yet straight-forward nature of the food. I especially loved the play on the pickles with a Berber/French/Korean flare. Everything in the restaurant was top notch quality at a very egalitarian price -- which really falls in line with the whole vibe of the restaurant itself.

I would highly recommend you visit when you can, and say hello to Chef Zadi for me.</review>

< review>
Great little par 3 course.  It has some length from the blue tees - not a bunch of overly short holes like some similar courses.Very lush and beautiful for the most part, but you'll encounter some road noise on some holes. Seemed to be well maintained, and the staff was great.  I like how there are yardage markers at each location, each tee box.  The course sets a premium on accuracy, and errant shots are easily lost forever.</review>

<Text>I cannot say enough good things about this course!   Beautiful, well maintained, very friendly staff, and incredibly reasonably priced!

It was my son's first time out and we rented clubs for me and him.  Clubs were very nice for rentals.  Course was perfect for him and challenging enough for me, too.  The greens were VERY good and the rest of the course was very well maintained... nice sand traps and some good water holes.  Very nice scenery, too.   Make sure you rent a cart, though... there was some distance between some of the holes (at $10 for a cart you can't go wrong). Good beer selection in the clubhouse, too.  All of the staff was very friendly although I must give a shout-out to David who was helping us at the end after our round and in the clubhouse.  Very friendly and helpful.  Gave a lot of good info about the course and the surrounding courses owned by the same management.
